Situation Not Eased After Rome Communique, Resolution Sought Outside League of Nations, British Government Likely to Disapprove 49

(Rome) Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's communique yesterday, aimed at the League of Nations, stated that Italy continues to have reasons to increase its forces on the Abyssinian border, claiming that the country is taking advantage of the League's delays to prepare for war against Italy, so Italy must continue to move troops there. The communique also outlined Mussolini's foreign policy, which included the following four points: (1) If Italy withdraws from the League of Nations, Italy believes it is the League of Nations' fault; (2) If the League of Nations takes no further hostile action, Italy will not withdraw; (3) Avoid expanding the scope of the Italian-Abyssinian dispute; (4) Italy's demand for the opening up of colonial territories must proceed regardless of world opinion. (National Telegraph, 28th)

(London) According to the Press Association today, without obtaining further details, Italy's recent communique cannot ease the current situation. The communique appears to be based on the erroneous view promoted by Italy that the Abyssinian case is actually a struggle between British and Italian interests in East Africa. However, British cabinet members have repeatedly declared that Britain has no selfish interests in Abyssinia and is acting solely as a member of the League of Nations, in accordance with the dispute with France. Whether Italy intends to negotiate and make military action unnecessary, or intends to negotiate an agreement with Britain on British interests in East Africa after it has become the master of Abyssinia, is still unknown. However, in the current situation, this proposal does not seem to have much value, as the former implies seeking a resolution outside the League of Nations, which the British government is unlikely to approve, and the latter will not avoid war in Abyssinia. (Reuters, 28th)

(Paris) Observers here and in several other European governments initially held a slim hope that Mussolini might be willing to negotiate at the last minute before the League of Nations Executive Council decides to impose sanctions on Italy. However, this hope has been dashed by the recent communique from the Italian government. The communique issued after the Italian cabinet meeting stated: "Italy does not wish to withdraw from the League of Nations until the League of Nations itself assumes full responsibility for taking action against Italy. Italy has notified the British government, informing it that Italy is prepared to negotiate an agreement with Britain in the future that does not harm Britain's legitimate interests in Central Africa." Rome calls this an appeal to Britain to reconsider its attitude towards Italy's legitimate demands and a direct invitation for Britain to participate in bilateral negotiations. These negotiations are likely to take place outside the League of Nations framework, but even the most optimistic observers in Paris do not believe that Britain will be induced to participate in direct negotiations with Rome outside the League of Nations. (Reuters, 29th)

Situation Tense, Focus of World Attention, Memel Election Begins Voting, Britain, France, and Italy Send Representatives to Monitor, German Propaganda Is Everywhere 53

Memel: The election in Memel began today. Voters crowded the polls, and there were occasional shootings. The election began at 8 am this morning and was originally scheduled to end at 8 pm tonight. However, during a special meeting of the Lithuanian cabinet, it was decided to amend the election law to extend the voting period until midnight or tomorrow due to the slow pace of voting. (Reuters, 29th)

Memel: The Memel parliament will hold elections tomorrow. The world's attention has never been greater than this time. Over 100 foreign journalists have arrived here. Diplomatic representatives from Britain, France, Italy, and other countries have arrived from Kovno to monitor the election. The atmosphere is tense on the streets. Lithuanian and German propaganda and advertisements are everywhere. There are 73 polling stations, each with ten ballot boxes. There are approximately 70,000 voters. Voting will begin at 8 am tomorrow and end at 8 pm. Each box can hold 70 votes. Each ballot has 189 items. To vote for the Memel Joint List, 29 items must be torn off, placed in an envelope, sealed, and dropped into the ballot box. All votes will be collected in Memel City on Sunday night. The election committee consists of four Lithuanians and one representative of the Memel Joint List. There are 140 vote counters. It is estimated that there are 2 million ballots to be counted, and the counting process will take approximately one month. (National Telegraph, 28th)

Britain, France, and Italy, the three countries guaranteeing the autonomy of the Memel region, are satisfied with the Lithuanian government's promises and believe that they have fulfilled their obligation to protect Memel's autonomy. In short, the task undertaken by Britain, France, and Italy is not to arbitrate disputes between Germany and Lithuania. In reality, there is no so-called dispute between Germany and Lithuania. However, Germany cannot stand idly by as Lithuania unilaterally undermines the autonomous system of Memel guaranteed by the great powers and disregards the people's rights guaranteed by the Memel autonomous constitution. Furthermore, the letter from Britain, France, and Italy to the Council of the League of Nations, advocating for the cessation of disturbances in the Memel region and the improvement of relations between Lithuania and Germany, should be directed at Lithuania, not Germany. If Lithuania faithfully fulfills its obligations, the disturbances in the Memel region will naturally cease, and relations between Germany and Lithuania can be expected to improve. "The Berliner Börsen-Zeitung" published a dispatch from its correspondent in Memel, stating, "Tomorrow's election is not just an election; it is a plebiscite for German citizens. All necessary consequences will be immediately apparent after the election." This statement is particularly noteworthy. (28th Havas Telegram)

Severe Flooding in Kasumigaura, Japan; Farmers Lament Hopeless Harvest 61

The farmers are lamenting incessantly. Meanwhile, the turbid river water has flowed into Lake Kasumigaura, causing it to flood increasingly. The fields in the four counties of Niihari, Inashiki, Namegata, and Kashima along the shore, where farmers had been rejoicing at the prospect of a satisfactory autumn harvest, suddenly turned into a swamp from the night of the 28th to the morning of the 29th as dikes collapsed everywhere. This is the worst disaster since the 41st year of Meiji (1908). The water level is still rising, rendering the all-night efforts to shore up the dikes futile and only increasing the extent of the damage. (29th Japan United Telegram)

The Flashpoint of the Tense Italo-Abyssinian Conflict; The Complete Story of the Walwal Incident 71

Rome Correspondence: The conflict between Italy and Abyssinia has become increasingly tense recently. This newspaper has been constantly publishing reports on the state of military preparedness on both sides. The reason for the conflict, as well as the pretext invoked by Italy, is the "Walwal Incident." From the emergence of the dispute to mediation efforts, to the proposal of arbitration, it has thus far failed to be resolved, becoming a prelude to the Italo-Abyssinian military buildup. Even if Italy has other ambitions to occupy the entirety of Abyssinia, (as the reporter described in detail in a dispatch sent to this newspaper on July 19th), the so-called "Walwal Incident" is merely an excuse for its military actions. However, this incident ultimately remains the flashpoint of the Italo-Abyssinian war, possessing historical value. By studying the beginning and end of this incident, one can also glimpse Italy's specific objectives in Abyssinia.

Walwal is located at the border between southeastern Abyssinia in Africa and northeastern Italian Somaliland. Twelve days before the incident (December 5th of last year), the Anglo-Abyssinian Boundary Demarcation Committee convened in Walwal (i.e., November 23rd of last year) to discuss the dispute between British Somaliland and the Ogaden region of Abyssinia. The natives of British Somaliland, seeking water and grazing land, often moved to the Ogaden region of Abyssinia to obtain springs and pastures, which had been the case for many years and was officially recognized by the supplementary agreement of May 1897. However, there were occasional conflicts between the two tribes, which were difficult to mediate. In order to implement the 1897 treaty and determine the boundaries between the two sides to prevent disputes, the Anglo-Abyssinian Joint Committee was established and decided to meet in Walwal for discussions. However, when the committee arrived, Italian troops were already stationed there, with fortifications flying the Italian flag. The site of the Anglo-Abyssinian Joint Committee was also frequently reconnoitered by Italian aircraft. At the time, the British side was very angry, but in order to avoid causing a serious dispute, it declared that it would temporarily withdraw to Ado pending negotiations. Therefore, when the conflict between Italy and Abyssinia occurred on December 5th, there were no third parties present to witness it, and the entire course of events became the focus of the dispute between the two countries. Both the Italian and Abyssinian sides held their own views as defenses, each pointing to the other as having provoked the conflict first and intentionally challenging them. Italy used this as an excuse to demand the occupation of the entire country of Abyssinia.

When discussing the responsibility for this incident, one key point needs to be determined: what country does Walwal belong to? According to the provisions of the 1908 treaty, all territories inhabited by natives near the coast should belong to Italy, and all lands in the Ogaden region and territories inhabited by natives near the Ogaden region should belong to Abyssinia. However, this relatively abstract provision cannot solve the actual boundary problem. Therefore, the two sides formed a committee and met in 1910 and 1911, but they dispersed without any results due to the wide divergence of opinions. However, the ethnic provisions in the 1908 treaty are very clear: "All lands in the Ogaden region and territories inhabited by natives near the Ogaden region shall belong to Abyssinia." Walwal is inhabited by the Ogaden natives, so it is self-evident to whom it belongs. Moreover, in addition to the 1908 treaty, there was another agreement between the two sides in that year (negotiated by Abyssinian King Menelik and Italian representative Nerazzini, and formally recognized by the Italian government in a telegram on September 3, 1897, but the text of the agreement was not made public). According to Abyssinia's note to the League of Nations on January 15th of this year, the two countries agreed that Italian Somaliland should be 180 miles from the coast of the Indian Ocean, parallel to the Jubaland River region to Bena Maredara. The Italian government also agreed to Menelik's suggestion to draw a "Arbitral Border Line" on the map within the 180-mile range, which Menelik himself signed and handed to Nerazzini to take back to the Roman government. Based on the above points, Abyssinia has more reason to possess Walwal. Abyssinia declared that Walwal is 200 miles from the coast and has the "Arbitral Border Line" drawn by Menelik, which clearly belongs to the Abyssinian side and is also territory within the Ogaden region. Whether based on the treaties of 1897 or 1908, Walwal is Abyssinian territory.

However, the Italian side also has its reasons. Italy's actual occupation of Walwal has lasted for more than five years. If the land is indeed Abyssinian territory, the Abyssinian government should have protested long ago, but no such statement has been seen in the past five years, which shows that Abyssinia is not the sovereign of the land. Since Walwal is already occupied territory of Italy, the attack by Abyssinian troops and "riotous masses" on the Italian side is an "act of aggression." If this "act of aggression" is not stopped, it will encourage illegal military attacks. According to the Italian military magazine's assessment, if both the 1897 treaty and the 1908 treaty are in effect, there will be three different boundary lines between Italy and Abyssinia. Therefore, the boundary line should be based on the latest treaty (1908), and Walwal, Wardair, and Damot should all belong to the Mijertein clan in Italian Somaliland. In addition, according to the 1885 treaty, Obbia is also within the Italian protected area and has the right to develop into the northeastern interior. Therefore, the wells near Walwal are also within the Italian territory.

After the Walwal Incident, the Abyssinian government requested arbitration based on the 1928 treaty. Italy demanded that the governor of Herar province in Abyssinia apologize, punish the Abyssinian perpetrators and their superiors, formally pay respect to the Italian flag in Walwal, and pay compensation of 20,000 gold pounds. Abyssinia then appealed to the League of Nations under Article 11 of the Covenant (December 14th of last year). Subsequently, because Italy expressed its willingness to reconcile, the League of Nations temporarily refrained from intervening. After several twists and turns in the negotiations between the two countries, the so-called neutral zone was established on March 4th (Gerlogubi-Ado-Walwal-Afdub are all neutral zones). However, Abyssinia hoped to resolve the entire border issue, while Italy only wanted to discuss matters limited to the Walwal incident. The opinions of the two sides diverged again. On March 17th, Abyssinia made a second appeal to the League of Nations, invoking Articles 15 and 10 of the Covenant. Therefore, the Italian government has sent a large army and military supplies to Africa, and the situation is becoming increasingly serious. On April 12th, while the Stresa Conference was in progress, the two governments also agreed to establish an arbitration committee based on the 1928 treaty. At that time, the Italian government, because its military preparations were not yet fully complete, adopted a policy of procrastination. It objected to Abyssinia's appointment of foreigners as arbitrators (one was the French lawyer M. de la Pradelle, and the other was the American Pitman B. Potter), and referred to it as an exposure of Abyssinia's lack of culture, as a respectable national government had no knowledgeable and capable person who could serve as a representative. But this was indeed the case, and the Italian government could not help but acknowledge it. The committee held its first meeting in the Netherlands on June 25th. However, because the opinions of the two sides were far apart (Abyssinia advocated for a complete resolution of the border issue, while Italy insisted on limiting the discussion to the Walwal incident), it was suspended on July 5th. Abyssinia then requested the League of Nations to appoint a fifth arbitrator because the four were divided into two camps and could not make a decision. The League of Nations met on August 3rd and decided to try to get the committee to continue, with two points on the agenda: (1) The committee does not need to discuss the question of who Walwal belongs to, but should discuss the Walwal incident; (2) The arbitrators should proceed quickly and appoint a fifth arbitrator. This case can be said to require compromise. The first point was to appease Italy, and the second point was to accommodate Abyssinia. On August 8th, it was decided to appoint the Greek Ambassador to France, Nikolas Politis, as the fifth arbitrator. After this, the representatives of Britain, France, and Italy held tripartite talks in Paris on August 16th, attempting to divide Abyssinia's interests among themselves, but because Italy's attitude was unacceptable to Britain, the result was a complete failure.

The entire course of the so-called Walwal Incident, from its occurrence to the present, has been described as follows. As the reporter has said before, this is merely an excuse for Italy's military actions to occupy Abyssinia. Therefore, before the case occurred, the Italian government already had a clear plan and early intentions. After the case occurred, the Italian government openly sent a large army to Africa to wash away the shame of Adwa (Italy was defeated by the Abyssinian army at Adwa in 1896) and seize the entirety of Abyssinia to gradually realize its fascist imperial ambitions. The so-called arbitration, the so-called reconciliation, and fundamentally the so-called Walwal Incident are, on the Italian side, merely tools for its actions. The concrete expression of its entire ambition can be seen in the editorial of the Italian People's Newspaper on July 31st (the newspaper was founded by Mussolini, and it is said that most of the editorials are written by Mussolini himself). Its tone is: "It is a fact that Abyssinia is full of oppressed slaves, but this is not the reason for Italy's military action. The racial issue is not a major reason, and the so-called cultural enrichment is not what Italy is concerned with. Italy's real purpose has only two absolutely undeniable points: first, the concrete needs of the Italian nation; second, ensuring the security of East Africa. To solve this problem, the entire matter must be discussed, and to expand influence or establish a protectorate, military action must accompany it. The East African security issue can only be resolved by Italy itself. All disputes between Italy and Abyssinia should be resolved militarily, which is not only simple but also reasonable. We will resolve this problem according to this only path, whether cooperating with the League of Nations, regardless of the League of Nations, or even opposing the League of Nations."

Nanchang Fire Prevention Week: Further Demonstration of Fire Extinguishing Grenades Achieves Remarkable Results and Boosts Sales 72

Nanchang Correspondence: Nanchang City's Fire Prevention Week, held on the 21st at the Provincial Stadium with a citizens' assembly and demonstrations of fire prevention, firefighting, and first aid, was previously reported. During the event, the Shanghai Dazhong Trading Company demonstrated its self-made fire extinguishing grenades. Due to hurried preparations and inadequate arrangements, coupled with the wood panels used in the demonstration, which contained extremely high levels of alum water, the effectiveness of the grenade's chemicals was neutralized, preventing it from achieving its intended effect. Subsequently, the Shanghai company received a telegram reporting the situation, expressing deep regret as the grenades had consistently demonstrated remarkable effectiveness in previous demonstrations across various locations. As a result, the company promptly dispatched a technician to Nanchang and, on the 23rd, constructed a large wooden structure at the public stadium for a continued demonstration. The event drew an audience of no less than ten thousand people. The wooden structure was divided into two sections, and fires were ignited simultaneously. The flames quickly soared into the sky, becoming too intense to approach. As the flames erupted from the roof, reaching heights of several dozen feet, a grenade was thrown into the fire by an observer. The fire was immediately extinguished, and within two minutes, all embers were completely gone. This was repeated three times, each time proving successful. The audience erupted in applause, praising the grenade's exceptional fire extinguishing capabilities, unlike anything they had ever seen. Since the 23rd, individuals from all sectors of Nanchang have been eagerly placing orders for the grenades at the Limin Commodity Circulation Agency, the designated distributor.

Hubei Provincial Government Dispatches Personnel to Survey Continuously Collapsing People's Dikes; Repairs Require a Budget of Nine Million Yuan 73

Hankou Correspondence: During the flooding disaster, eight or nine out of ten people's dikes along the Jianghan area of Hubei Province collapsed. The counties had just finished repairing the breaches, which cost a total of 4.6 million yuan. Unexpectedly, not long after, the autumn floods arrived, and the dikes that had been spared in the first instance, as well as those that had been successfully repaired, collapsed again. Currently, authorities estimate that, based on the original plan to use labor relief for repairs, a total of over 9 million yuan will be required, doubling the initial budget. A telegram has been sent to the central government, earnestly requesting the advance release of the 3 million yuan pledged to facilitate commencement of work. Simultaneously, the Department of Civil Affairs, the Department of Construction, the Jianghan Engineering Bureau, and the Water Disaster Relief General Association have been instructed to select technical and administrative personnel to conduct on-site surveys in various counties. The survey committee members were announced by the provincial government on the 28th through an order, including Shen Jiqing and Yu Xishou for Huangmei and Guangji counties, Guo Xu and Gao Honghuan for Qichun and Peishui counties, Wei Yafan, Peng Yajie, and Lu Shigu for Huanggang and Jiayu counties, Wu Songqiao and Zhang Nixuan for Hankou City and Hanyang County, Yu Chuanzhou and Zhang Lutai for Xiaogan and Huangpi counties, Zhu Youyou and Wang Sichang for Yingcheng and Yunmeng counties, Chen Ying and Sun Shi for Tianmen and Hanchuan counties, Zhang Yuchen and Yao Zhi for Mianyang and Qianjiang counties, Qu Daozong and Song Ziming for Jiangling and Jianli counties, Luo Jin and Zhang Youguang for Shishou and Gongan counties, Xia Fulan and Wang Jiechen for Songzi and Zhijiang counties, Li Shuxin and Chen Tiezhen for Yidu and Yichang counties, Deng Zhirui and Lei Mengsu for Jingyou and Zhongxiang counties, Deng Shi and Pan Kangguo for Yicheng and Jingmen counties, and Zhao Zhihui and Bao Yaoding for Liyang and Guanghua counties. Survey Standards: (A) Survey Standards for People's Embankment Projects: (1) People's Dikes Related to Main Dikes: 1. Those directly connected to main dikes; 2. Those within the main dikes with the function of divider dikes; (2) Important people's dikes and embankments related to a large portion of a county's farmland or multiple counties; (3) City walls used as dikes; (B) Estimation of Projects, divided into the following two points: (1) Projects to restore the original state; (2) Projects to raise and reinforce the original embankment in the future; 1. The height and thickness of main dikes should be estimated using two methods: one based on a height 1.5 meters above the flood level and simultaneously leveling the inner and outer slopes; the other based on a height 2 "Shi Chi" above the highest flood level, only leveling the inner slope.

Estimation standards will depend on the amount of funds available to determine the height of the standard; 2. People's dikes within main dikes that function as divider dikes should be as high as the main dikes; embankments outside the main dikes that impede floodwaters should not be estimated; those that do not impede floodwaters should be estimated at a height 1 meter lower than the main dike; (C) Personnel Assignment Method: (1) The provincial government will dispatch 18 engineering personnel to conduct surveys in the 36 counties and cities with people's dikes; (2) The Water Disaster Relief General Association will dispatch personnel to jointly conduct surveys in the disaster-stricken counties with dikes. (28th)

Hankou Chamber of Commerce Requests Improvement of Business Tax; Compiles a Document on Various Industries and Proposes Four Measures 74

Hankou Correspondence: Amidst natural and man-made disasters, Hankou's commerce is declining daily. Various industry associations believe that the heavy burden of taxes and levies is a major contributing factor to this phenomenon. They have requested the Chamber of Commerce to forward their concerns to the government and improve the business tax. The Chamber of Commerce convened a general meeting of industry representatives to discuss the matter, resulting in four points: exemption, deferral, reduction, or even complete abolishment, replaced by other taxes. The Chamber of Commerce has submitted these proposals to the Ministry of Finance for review, stating in essence: "Hankou's commercial sector has suffered greatly in recent years due to the impact of natural and man-made disasters. Commerce has declined significantly compared to previous years. In the spring and summer of this year, it was first shaken by silver market fluctuations, leading to a sudden financial panic, followed by a major flood disaster, which caused disruptions in cargo transportation. As a result, accounts receivable for various industries have been difficult to collect, while payments owed for goods have been hard to meet. Although the government has stipulated a method allowing goods to be mortgaged to banks for loans, the strict regulations imposed by banks have made it difficult to provide widespread relief. Even now, following the Shanghai precedent of supporting industry and commerce, a request has been made to the government for the allocation of a large sum of debt financing to provide remedies, which various industries rely on for survival and which the government is expected to approve and implement. However, the back-and-forth of documents will inevitably take time, making it like waiting for rain in the west river to revive dried-up fish, which is too slow to be of immediate help. The current difficulties faced by various industries have already been mentioned. However, bearing various taxes and levies has made the commercial sector unable to bear the burden. Among these, the business tax is the most burdensome for businesses and the public. The opinions of various industries regarding the business tax are detailed below: (1) Request for Exemption: The business tax was initially established to offset the Likin tax. However, customs duties have already increased. The provincial government's financial needs can be covered by allocations from the central government. Furthermore, Shanghai does not have this tax. Considering the special circumstances of Wuhan, requesting exemption based on precedent is reasonable. This is the first point. (2) Request for Temporary Deferral: If the request for exemption cannot be achieved, given the severity of this year's disaster, which is more severe than the major flood of 1931, the precedent of deferring land taxes should be followed. A request should be made to defer the unpaid business tax for various industries this year until the next year when commerce improves, and then reassess the situation to schedule collection, allowing the commercial sector to alleviate some of its burden and preventing the people's livelihoods from being on the verge of collapse. This is the second point. (3) Request for Reduction of Tax Rates: Regardless of whether the measures for exemption and deferral can be achieved, the current business tax rate in this province is excessively high, and there is an urgent need to reduce it. The original tax rates were considered moderate, but after changing to a three-tiered tax system, the increase has been more than several times. For example, the tax on cotton was originally only 0.25%, but was later changed to 1%. After repeated requests for reduction, it was still changed to 0.8%. It is difficult to list all other instances of burdens and difficulties. Furthermore, even when the tax on cotton was 0.2%, other provinces did not have such high taxes. This severely hinders commerce. A request for reduction should be made in advance. This is the third point. (4) Request for Improvement of Tax Collection Methods: While requesting a reduction in the business tax rate, the standards for taxation should also be improved to facilitate implementation. If based on the "Che Ji" method, it would lead to excessive taxes on empty goods, causing unbearable hardship for businesses and the public. If based on the current method, actual amounts would be paid and collected, benefiting both officials and businesses. All statements made are supported by various industries. If maintained, they should be implemented uniformly. In addition to the business tax, if there is a better tax system, such as changing to a production and sales tax or a unified tax, as long as it benefits the public and does not disturb businesses, various industries would be happy to support it. A request is made to modify it accordingly. This is the fourth point. The Chamber of Commerce has verified that all the above-mentioned situations are factual. A request is hereby submitted for review and compliance." (28th)

Japanese Side Actively Promotes Economic Cooperation in North China; Various Investigation Teams Come to China for Research and Study; South Manchuria Railway Company Expands Tianjin Office Organization 75

Tianjin Correspondence: The South Manchuria Railway Company's economic investigation of North China seems to have completed its first phase, and the second phase is now beginning. Naka Tokio, the head of the South Manchuria Railway Company's Economic Research Department, responsible for the investigation mission, arrived in Tianjin last week from Shenyang with five team members. After staying for one day, they went to Zhangbei, Guanhua, Zhuolu, and Wande to further investigate mineral resources. After working there, they will go to northern Shanxi to investigate special minerals. The Japanese side believes that the development of the Xuanhua Longyan Iron Mine in Chahar Province requires more than 10 million in capital, so careful consideration is needed on how to exploit it. Doihara, the head of the Kwantung Army Special Service Agency in Shenyang, who is in charge of the Sino-Japanese cooperation plan, took a plane to Chahar on the 23rd to investigate, and plans to go to Shanxi with Colonel Matsui, the Kwantung Army's military liaison officer in Chahar, to discuss economic development and make decisions on military planning. However, there is a lot of skepticism in Japan about investing in and economically cooperating with North China, and capitalists are hesitant to move forward. Even the East Development Company and the East Cotton Company think that it is too little, so the research groups continue to come, one is to collect materials for all parties to study. Within this week, two groups will visit Tianjin. One is the Oriental Association organized within the East Development Company, consisting of Chairman Kawase Tatsuo, Secretary Yamamoto Kitayo, mining expert Tamura Yoshiaki, Ueda Kiyono expert Kimura Yu, etc. It conducts inspections of the textile, industrial, commercial and export trade. After staying in Tianjin for one day, they will go to Shanxi and Suiyuan. The other is the Noda Economic Research Institute, led by Noda Yutaka, accompanied by Mitarai Tatsuo, and Yamazaki Yasuzumi, the owner of the Yamazaki Research Institute in Osaka and an expert in economic commentary at the Tokyo Yomiuri Shimbun, and seven others. They are collecting various materials on industry, commerce, water conservancy, and mines. After staying in Tianjin for two days, they will go to Ping, transfer to Chahar, and then return to Shandong and Hebei for investigation. On our side, in addition to the Hebei Economic Association recently established in Ping, private organizations in Tianjin such as Gao Lingxiao's Association for Rescuing the Economy of North China, Niu Chuanqi's East Asia Economic Association, and the East Asia Tonghui Trading Company initiated by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and prepared by Pan Yansheng Bian Shoujing, etc., all ignore the benefits and want to take the opportunity to introduce foreign investment and invest in the industry and commerce of North China to make profits. However, the Japanese side believes that the persons in charge are not central figures in industry and commerce and are not very trustworthy. Except for the East Asia Tonghui Trading Company, the authorities are afraid that it will play a role and have banned it from being established. The remaining two organizations exist in name only. However, recently Gong Xinzhan (former Minister of Interior of the Northern Government) and Niu Chuanqi, Shen Tongshi, Gao Lingwei and others organized the North China Economic Association, which has the same nature as the East Asia Economic Association and is responsible for investigation and introduction. It has been approved for registration by the Tianjin Municipal Government and may be more sound than other organizations in the future, and more events will be handled. It is also reported that the South Manchuria Railway Company, in order to promote economic cooperation methods, decided to expand the organization of the Tianjin Office on November 1, and set up four sections: investigation, general affairs, business, and development, and an economic advisory department attached to it, which will take contact with the Kwantung Army Department and the North China Garrison Department. The Pingqingji three offices are all under the jurisdiction of the Tianjin office. The scale is several times larger than before, and the responsibility is not limited to the railway itself. This is something to pay attention to. (27th)

All winning bonds are scheduled to be redeemed for principal and interest starting from October 1st at the Shanghai and Hangzhou branches of the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank and the governments of various counties in Anhui. The meeting was adjourned at about 4:00 p.m.

League of Nations Health Expert Dr. Stampar to Depart for Yunnan Tomorrow to Assist Yao Yongzheng's Malaria Prevention Program 88

It is reported by the "Shen Shi She" that Dr. Stampar, a health expert from the League of Nations, after arriving in China, traveled south to Sichuan Province last year for an inspection. He expressed his approval and deep hope for the solutions achieved by the provincial health authorities in diagnosing and treating malignant malaria. This time, the Ministry of Health is sending personnel south, traveling through Guizhou and Guangxi to Yunnan for investigation. After careful research, it was learned that the miasma in that area is a type of malignant malaria. The Ministry of Health, in response to the request of Long Yun, the chairman of Yunnan Province, has continued to dispatch Yao Yongzheng to design prevention and control measures for the province and has also invited Dr. Stampar to assist in the south. After accepting the invitation, Dr. Stampar decided to depart for Hong Kong on the first of next month, taking the route through Annam to Yunnan to assist. It is also heard that Dr. Stampar intends to report the results of his work to the international health conference to be held in Singapore next year.

Cultivating Cinchona Trees

The area along Simao and Honghe in Yunnan Province has fertile land and a favorable climate, but it suffers greatly from the effects of miasma, leading to the abandonment of land, which is a great pity. The provincial Department of Construction, recognizing that cinchona trees can not only be used for general medicinal purposes but also can control this type of miasma, attempted to purchase seeds several years ago. After seven trial plantings, all failed. However, they were not discouraged by the failures and purchased seeds from the Kalajida area of India at a cost of 2,800 yuan. They dispatched personnel to the Honghe riverside area for another trial planting, which was successful. Currently, there are already over 10,000 planted trees, no different from those in India. The Department of Construction plans to further expand the planting area along the Honghe riverside to various places in the Simao interior.

Research on Medicine

Guangxi is located near the tropics, with many mountains, rivers, and trees, which are ideal for the breeding of malarial mosquitoes. Therefore, malaria is extremely prevalent in the province. Although there are no accurate statistics on the annual death rate from malaria, the number must be very high. People generally attribute this epidemic to miasma and mostly resign themselves to fate. People from other provinces also regard Guangxi as a miasma-ridden area, turning pale at the mention of it and treating it as a dangerous path. The provincial authorities deeply feel that the prevention and treatment of this disease are extremely important and have specifically ordered the provincial medical college to conduct research to find the true cause so that methods of prevention and treatment can be devised. After detailed field research by the college, it was discovered that the so-called miasma disease is actually a type of malignant malaria. Now that the truth has been discovered, prevention and treatment are easier to initiate. The province is currently preparing to launch a large-scale anti-malaria campaign. At the same time, Dr. Zeng Guangfang, who previously came to Guangxi to investigate medicinal plants, has already left Guangxi and returned to Shanghai. Yesterday, specific orders were issued to the Guangxi Agricultural Experiment Station and the Baise District Agricultural and Forestry Demonstration Farm to collect samples of white tree oil, two types of tree bark and leaves of the large-leaf tree, and medicinal plant specimens such as "Aina Xiang" (Camphorosma), which will be transported to Shanghai and given to Dr. Zeng for use in testing medicinal materials.

Research on Nuisance Mosquitoes

Malignant malaria has recently been discovered in Minhang and other places near Shanghai, and the spread is quite rapid. The situation is very dangerous. The Shanghai Suburban Mosquito Research Unit, established by the Listers Institute of Preventive Medicine in Gaoqiao, is currently focusing its efforts on this work, and the results are said to be exceptionally good.

Amidst Reports of Floods in Various Regions, Abundant Harvests of Indica Rice in Hunan and Anhui Provinces, Harvesting Already Completed, New Rice to Be Sold Early Next Month, Rice Prices in Shanghai Decline Due to Congestion of Sources 93

This autumn, the Yellow River flooded, causing devastation in provinces such as Hebei, Shandong, Henan, Hubei, and other provinces, with fields submerged and huts turned into ruins. The disaster is more severe than that of 1931. Amidst the reports of these floods, Hunan, Jiangxi, and Anhui provinces have all reported bumper harvests of late-season indica rice. Rice prices in Shanghai have fallen due to the large number of goods arriving from various regions. The details are as follows:

Abundant Harvests of Late-Season Rice in Hunan, Anhui, and Jiangxi

Jiangxi, Hunan, and Anhui provinces are well-known areas for indica rice production in China, with considerable harvests each year. Since the beginning of autumn this year, floods have occurred in the Yellow River basin. Except for the counties along the tributaries of the Yellow River, which suffered slight losses, the late-season rice in other counties in the three provinces has achieved a bumper harvest, with yields increasing by 25% compared to last year. The farmers have already completed harvesting, and after milling, the rice will be fully available for sale early next month.

Congestion of Rice Shipments, Rice Prices Decline in Shanghai

Recently, the weather has been mild, and the rural areas have stopped. Rice from the interior is being transported to Shanghai in a continuous stream, causing rice prices to decline in recent days. The current price for Grade A rice is 12.1 yuan, Grade B is 11 yuan, and Grade C is 10.23 yuan. Although the prices of foreign rice are rising in their countries of origin, the inventory in the rice market is limited, and the congestion of "Du Rice" (rice smuggled from Southeast Asia) is causing the market prices to remain stable. Currently, Saigon rice is priced at 10.04 yuan per stone, and "Xiao Jiao" rice is priced at 9.56 yuan per stone.

Xintong Bank Held Shareholders' Meeting Yesterday, Resolved to Begin Liquidation Tomorrow 96

After Xintong Commercial and Savings Bank suspended operations, it held an emergency shareholders' meeting at the bank at 2:00 PM yesterday. The number of shareholders and shares present both exceeded the majority. A chairman was elected to open the meeting and discuss solutions to the aftermath. After repeated discussions, there were no good solutions, and a vote was taken. It was unanimously resolved that under the current circumstances, it was impossible to resume operations, and it was approved to dissolve immediately. It was decided to begin liquidation on October 1st and to appoint lawyer Wu Guochang and accountant Zhao Zuwei as liquidators to handle the liquidation matters with full authority. All matters to be handled or decided thereafter will be the responsibility of the chairman of the board to process, shareholders gave the chairman full power so that it can be completed quickly, the meeting adjourned. According to a "Xin Sheng She" reporter's inquiry, the bank owes over 92,000 yuan in savings deposits. It has 45,000 yuan in reserve funds deposited with the Central Bank, which can be used to repay customers after withdrawal. There is also a property pledge on Yu Garden Road, which can be converted into 27,000 yuan in silver, and shares in Qian Yi Ji's property, which can be converted into over 10,000 yuan. There are also other pledges, so the savings deposits can be fully repaid. In addition, the commercial deposits owed are no more than 2,000 yuan, and the collection of debts and repayment of deposits will not be a problem. In terms of pledges, there is a transfer of property, with little difference in value.

Shanghai District Court Will Accept Meetings with Unindicted Defendants, Chief Judge Zhong Agreed to Follow Common Practice 103

Since last year, Shanghai District Court has imposed special restrictions on criminal defendants in detention, prohibiting lawyers from meeting with them before indictment. This practice is unprecedented in other courts. The Shanghai Bar Association has repeatedly negotiated, but without success. Recently, Shen Junru, a standing committee member of the association, again met with Chief Judge Zhong Shangbin, arguing that this system not only sets a unique example for the national courts, but also causes inconvenience to the court, litigants, and lawyers. After sincere consultation, Zhong agreed to follow common practice and allow lawyers to meet with detainees, eliminating the previous special restrictions. Therefore, lawyers are now able to meet with detained suspects who have not been indicted without any obstacles.

Ningbo Association Supports Zhejiang Relief, All-Zhejiang Relief Association Petitions for Commendation, Requesting the National Government to Award a Plaque to Show Encouragement, Based on Government's Regulations on Rewarding Relief Organizations 105

The Ningbo Association in Shanghai is a group of Ningbo people in Shanghai, which has always been known for its efforts in supporting charitable and public welfare undertakings in their hometown. In 1930, when Zhejiang Province suffered a flood, the Zhejiang people in Shanghai organized the All-Zhejiang Relief Association. In 1934, when there was a drought, they reorganized the Jiaxu All-Zhejiang Relief Association. Both times, the association served as the office, and many of its members participated in relief work and made tireless efforts to raise relief funds. It is now learned that the chairman and committee members of the Jiaxu All-Zhejiang Relief Association, Chu Huiseng, Zhang Xiaolin, Wang Xiaoji, and others, believe that the association should be rewarded for its support of relief efforts to encourage others, and therefore, based on the government's regulations on rewarding relief organizations, they petitioned Chairman Lin of the National Government for an award. The text states, "Petition regarding the two times of raising relief funds for the Zhejiang disaster, relying on the support of the Ningbo Association in Shanghai, requesting the awarding of a plaque to show commendation and encouragement. Upon investigation, Zhejiang Province suffered a severe flood in 1930 and a drought in 1934. The Zhejiang people in Shanghai organized the All-Zhejiang Relief Association and the Jiaxu All-Zhejiang Relief Association, which were organized by the Zhejiang people in Shanghai, and they handled the Zhejiang relief efforts under the Central Relief Committee with some success. Hundreds of thousands of dying disaster victims were able to temporarily survive. Looking back, although various philanthropists actively donated to raise funds, the Ningbo Association in Shanghai was the first to care for their hometown and provided the strongest support. All the two disaster agreements used the association's hall as the venue, and it provided various spiritual and material assistance. Its dedication to public service is a model for general community organizations. Now that the association's operations are coming to an end, remembering the two periods of continuous effort, it is believed that the association's contribution cannot be ignored. Therefore, in accordance with the government's regulations on rewarding relief organizations, we respectfully submit this petition to the government for approval, requesting that a plaque be awarded to commend the association and encourage others, which would be greatly appreciated."

The Jisheng Hui (Relief Society) - Detailed Record of Famine Relief Grain Distribution in Tianmen 107

The Chinese Jisheng Hui (Relief Society) recently received a detailed report from its relief directors in Hubei Province, Hou Yongde and Qian Xinru, from the disaster area of Tianmen. The report stated: (1) The Tianmen County area is mostly plains with a dense population of over 800,000 residents. Over 600,000 have been affected by the disaster, a situation of unprecedented severity. (2) The society initially remitted 3,000 yuan and Han-style currency of 2,000 yuan, totaling 5,000 yuan. This was used to purchase 350 *zu* of rice at about 10 yuan per *fan cheng dou* plus one *liang* (unit of weight, approximately 50 grams). 350 *dan* of broad beans were purchased at about 3.5 yuan per *shi*. This totaled 4,725 yuan, with the remaining 200+ yuan reserved for transportation to disaster areas in the western villages. Each adult received one *sheng* of rice and beans, while each child received half a *sheng*, measured using the *fan cheng dou* plus one *dou* measurement. This was enough to provide for 30,000 adults and 10,000 children. (3) One *fan cheng dou* plus one *dou* is equal to 1.6 *han dou*. With rice and beans figured together, each *shi* costs approximately 4 yuan. Broken rice in Hankou is priced similarly, but broken rice is much less effective at satisfying hunger compared to regular rice and broad beans. (4) On the 20th of this month, an inspection of the first district of the city (several miles from the urban village of Yanglinkou) was made, walking dozens of miles, and only 240 households were inspected. In the future, it is planned to divide the work into three districts (the first and eighth districts of the western villages, and the fifth district of this village) to expedite the process. Villages are spread far apart, with each village consisting of a few dozen households, requiring several miles of travel to reach the next village. Most villages are submerged in water, requiring boats to cross. In many places, travel by land or water is impossible due to the completely muddy conditions, rendering efforts futile. (5) Due to the severity of the disaster, distribution cannot wait until the complete inspection is finished. Once several dozen people are identified, distribution is carried out. Local *baojia* leaders assist in distribution. After distribution, the amount of rice and beans distributed is calculated and announced in the district. (6) In many remote and difficult-to-reach areas, disaster victims are found sick and lying among broken walls and crumbling tiles, nearing death. When questioned, they can only weakly reply with the words "Yu a" (I am), unable to speak further, bringing tears to the eyes. Being fellow humans, their suffering is extreme. An act of compassion and virtue, donating one yuan can save a life, saving others is saving oneself. (7) A large batch of disaster relief medicine was previously received, including 2,500 packets of dysentery powder and 4,500 bottles of Jisheng Dan (pills). Taoist priest Hou carried two large packages of Changchun Dan (longevity pills), which were distributed as needed. Dysentery is widespread, and the medicine is particularly effective. Requests for more are pouring in, urging for more to be sent urgently. (8) On the way from Hankou to Tianmen, the area beyond Liujia was like traveling in the ocean, with no end in sight. The scene of vast areas of land submerged in water is imaginable. It is often said that nine out of ten houses are empty, but now there is no home to return to, no house to be empty. (9) The disaster area of Tianmen is vast, and the current relief funds are just a drop in the bucket. We can only try our best to inspect the poorest, ensuring that every drop counts. How much can a small donation save? We earnestly request all philanthropists to quickly allocate large amounts of relief funds so that dying disaster victims can have their lives extended. Their eyes are filled with hope, and their hearts are breaking with anxiety. It is reported that the Society has added 1,000 yuan in relief funds. Yesterday, the Chinese and Foreign Relief Society sent 5,000 yuan in relief funds to jointly administer emergency relief. Each of the two societies sent a relief worker, Zheng Shouyong and Gu Yabin, to jointly manage the operation, bringing with them a large batch of relief medicine, and departing immediately.

Chinese Association for the Protection of Children – Public Banquet for Ms. Ding Shujing – Ms. Ding Reports on the International Conference on Family Education – Our Proposals Were All Adopted and Received an Exhibition Certificate 108

At 11 a.m. the day before yesterday (28th), the staff of the Chinese Association for the Protection of Children held a public banquet at the Hong Kong Road Navy YMCA in honor of Ms. Ding Shujing, who had recently traveled overseas on behalf of the Association to participate in the International Conference on Family Education held in Brussels, Belgium. She had worked diligently and brought honor to her country abroad, and the banquet was a warm welcome and show of respect. Attendees included Association staff Zhang Yueru, Han Chao, Zhao Jian, Liu Yide, Ding Bingnan, and heads of affiliated institutions Yao Shuwen, Huang Huiguang, Wang Baozhu, Wang Zhenchang, and others, totaling over twenty people. Chen Zhengfan delivered a welcoming speech on behalf of everyone, stating that Ms. Ding had departed on May 25th, representing not only the Chinese Young Women’s Christian Association (YWCA) in the World YWCA Executive Committee Enlarged Meeting, but also representing the Association in the Fifth International Conference on Family Education in Brussels, Belgium. Her mission was of great importance. The International Conference on Family Education was initiated by the Belgian educator Dr. De Jost, with the aim of bringing together representatives from various countries and outstanding figures in family education to conduct in-depth discussions to promote family education in various countries. Its significance is undoubtedly great. Ms. Ding's long journey, despite the hardships, made many contributions on behalf of our country at the conference, which not only brought honor to our country but also learned from the strengths of others and compensated for our weaknesses. Her contributions will undoubtedly have a significant impact on the future of family education in our country. Today, we are holding this banquet to express our warm welcome and respect to Ms. Ding, and we are extremely pleased, etc. Ms. Ding Shujing then gave a reply speech, stating that she had been abroad for four months, first taking the Siberian Railway from Vladivostok, passing through Soviet Russia, and arriving directly in Berlin, Germany. After disembarking, she inspected Hitler's rule in that country, then traveled to Geneva, Switzerland, to attend the Enlarged Meeting of the World YWCA Executive Committee. From July 31st to August 4th, she attended the Fifth International Conference on Family Education in Brussels, Belgium. She gained a wealth of practical materials that could be used as a reference for compatriots. Over 300 representatives from 23 countries including England, America, France, Germany, Italy, Belgium, and Switzerland attended the Family Education Conference. In addition to herself, the Chinese delegation included Mr. Ling Qihan, Chargé d'Affaires of the Chinese Legation in Belgium. At the opening ceremony, female students from Brussels participated in performances, and the Queen of Belgium personally opened the ceremony and shook hands with representatives from various countries. However, within a few days, the Queen tragically died in a car accident. The incident was met with deep mourning. The theme of the conference was "Training for a Healthy Personality," which was divided into seven groups for discussion. The Bankruptcy Law Takes Effect Tomorrow – Debtors Who Cannot Pay Their Debts Can Apply for Reconciliation or Bankruptcy According to the Law 122

The Bankruptcy Law promulgated by the National Government on July 17th of this year, as ordered on July 19th, will take effect on October 1st. Its implementation law was also promulgated earlier on July 18th. All debtors who cannot pay their debts can apply for debt repayment via the reconciliation or bankruptcy procedures stipulated in the law. Whether it is a civil or commercial matter, it can be applied. Details are noted as follows:

Provisions of the Bankruptcy Law

The provisions of the Bankruptcy Law consist of three chapters and 159 articles. Detailed regulations are stipulated regarding the responsibilities of bankrupts or reconciliators, reconciliation procedures, reconciliation agencies, reconciliation methods, declaration and effect of bankruptcy, composition and management of the bankrupt estate, bankruptcy claims, creditors' meetings, distribution of the bankrupt estate, and termination of bankruptcy and restoration of rights. The second section of the second chapter, which stipulates the reconciliation methods of the Chamber of Commerce, is particularly convenient and is a characteristic of Chinese bankruptcy law. In addition to this law, there is also the Implementation Law of the Bankruptcy Law, which has a total of six articles. The text of the law will be published in the tenth issue of the Commercial Monthly.

History of the Bankruptcy Law

Yan E'sheng, Secretary of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, said that China's bankruptcy law began with the Bankruptcy Law of the 32nd year of the Guangxu reign, which was compiled by Wu Tingfang and Shen Jiaben and had a total of 69 articles. It was only applicable to merchants. In the 33rd year of the Guangxu reign, Article 40 of the law stipulated that the percentage of repayment should be handled uniformly for all creditors, which was inconsistent with the usual practice of first paying foreign debts, then official debts, and then proportionally distributing to Chinese and foreign merchants. It was opposed by the Ministry of Commerce and explicitly repealed. In the fourth year of the Republic of China, the Beijing Law Revision Office drafted a bankruptcy law, and in the 23rd year, the Judicial and Administrative Department of the National Government also drafted a bankruptcy law, but neither became formal law. In August of the 23rd year, because adjudicators often encountered bankruptcy cases but had no clear legal basis, the Ministry of Industry and the Ministry of Justice jointly drafted the Provisional Regulations for the Settlement of Merchant Debts, which were submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and filed by the Central Political Conference. However, its application was limited to merchants. After the Bankruptcy Law takes effect on October 1st, according to Article 5 of the Implementation Law of the Bankruptcy Law, the Provisional Regulations for the Settlement of Merchant Debts will simultaneously lose their effectiveness.

Deliberations by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce stated that the Bankruptcy Law stipulates a section on Chamber of Commerce reconciliation. In the future, when merchants are unable to pay their debts, they must first request Chamber of Commerce reconciliation. The recently handled reconciliation case of the Huaying Pharmacy is an example of this. Therefore, in addition to the various procedures prescribed by law, detailed measures are being discussed to accept handling procedures.

Shanghai West Shenjiatang: Robber Shoots and Wounds Shen Jingting 124

In the desolate area of Jiangjiatang, south of Hongqiao Town in western Shanghai, bandits frequently appear. Yesterday morning at 4:40 AM, more than ten robbers speaking in a mixed foreign accent and wearing short clothes (four of them carrying pistols) suddenly broke into the residence of Shen, a current technician at the Municipal Land Bureau, in Shenjiatang. The entire Shen family was awakened from their dreams and forced into one room by the robbers, who forbade them from making any noise. The robbers then rummaged through chests and cabinets, searching arbitrarily. Next, they broke into the home of Shen Pinfang, a neighbor. At that time, Shen's cousin, Shen Jingting (45 years old), had just returned home from the Huangjia Garden. Upon hearing about the robbery in his family's home, he disregarded everything, leaped onto the robber acting as a lookout outside the door from behind, and captured him. The robber pulled out a pistol and fired two shots at Shen Jingting, one hitting his right shoulder and the other his right leg. After being wounded, Shen fell to the ground. Hearing the gunshots outside, the other robbers did not dare to stay longer and fled north with the loot. At that moment, Huo Fengchi, the police chief of the Hongqiao Town police station, was leading a patrol when he heard the gunshots. He rushed to the scene to pursue the robbers, but they had already gone far. Therefore, he sent the wounded Shen Jingting to the Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road overnight for treatment. It is reported that the bullet in his right shoulder has not yet been removed, and his life is in critical condition. The homeowner has filed a loss report with the relevant Public Security Bureau for investigation.

They are inexpensive and of good quality, and customers are welcome. The bureau is offering a custom weaving service specifically for customers as a souvenir.

Most people advocate for a partial modification of the unit names in the current weights and measures law. 2. Most main units advocate for using meters, acres, and liters, and a few advocate for using "mike-li" (meters-kilograms-liters). Dancer Ren Aina Sues Li Yuzao for Seduction: Abandoned After Getting Pregnant, Gave Birth to a Daughter: Trial Opened the Other Day, Defendant Did Not Appear 139

Shao, a woman named Ren Dong, is 40 years old. She only had one daughter, named Aina, who is now 19 years old. Li Yuzao, the son of a prominent family from Qibao Town, was 22 years old. He fell in love with her at first sight. After several meetings, they had a physical relationship. Soon, Aina became pregnant and stopped working as a dancer. On July 19th of this year, she gave birth to a daughter. However, misfortune struck. Li Yuzao abandoned Ren Aina and ignored her. Aina could no longer tolerate it. Accompanied by her mother, Ren Dong, she filed a complaint with the criminal court of the local court, accusing Li Yuzao of interfering with her family and seduction. The second time they met at the Yangzi Hotel on the fourth floor. After that, they easily met at various locations. When the plaintiff's mother returned to her hometown on business, the defendant even became a frequent visitor to the plaintiff's home (Chongli, Malang Road, Lafayette Road), which was witnessed by many. The defendant deceived the plaintiff due to her youth, falsely claiming that he was not married and willing to marry the plaintiff. The plaintiff was secretly delighted, thinking that she had found someone to rely on for life, and did not suspect anything else. Unexpectedly, the defendant recently sent a letter scolding the plaintiff in every possible way, intending to break up with her. The plaintiff suddenly woke up from her dream and realized that she had been deceived. By this time, the defendant's promise to marry her had vanished into thin air. As a last resort, she had to file a lawsuit according to the law, requesting an investigation. After receiving the complaint, the court issued a subpoena, but the defendant did not appear. The other day, Judge Wu Deying held a trial, but the defendant still failed to appear. Only the plaintiff and her mother appeared in court and testified about what happened. How Did the Boat Crew Member Drown? Police Station Summons for Thorough Investigation: Impersonating Public Officials Is Suspicious: Boat Owner Evades, Disappears Without a Trace 140

Gong Haigen, a local from No. 3, Qianjiazhai, Yangsi Township, Pudong, owned a pier boat and hired Yao A'mei, a local, as the captain to supervise the crew in transporting goods. On the afternoon of the 19th of this month at 4:00 PM, Gong was playing mahjong in a teahouse near the pier. Yao needed money for expenses on the boat and went to the teahouse to ask Gong for one yuan. Gong refused, saying he had no money. Yao saw a five-yuan banknote on Gong's table and insisted on getting change to pay him. The two began to argue and then wrestled to the boat by the port, resulting in a major conflict. Somehow, Yao suddenly fell into the river and died. The next day, the body floated near the area. After the family retrieved it, two people on bicycles resembling public officials arrived at the scene and instructed the family to collect the body first and wait for verification. The deceased's family followed their instructions and prepared a coffin for burial. After several days, the family members became concerned that Gong had not taken any action and had not mentioned anything about the deceased's affairs. The deceased's aunt, Zhang Yao (72 years old), went to Gong's house to make a scene, but it was to no avail. Although this case originated in the countryside and was not immediately known to the police, the news spread further and further. Yesterday morning, the Tangqiao police learned of the incident and summoned the deceased's wife, Jiang Min (17 years old), the deceased's father, Yao Bojiang (56 years old), and the injured aunt, Zhang Yao, for questioning. They all claimed that after the deceased was knocked down by Gong, they retrieved the body shortly afterward. Two people claiming to be from the local court instructed them to collect the body, so they did not dare to resist. When Yao Min went to Gong's house to negotiate the deceased's affairs, he was also attacked and injured. The police chief believed that the local court would never send two people on bicycles to verify the body without first instructing the local bailiff to report it. It was clear that the two unknown men were impersonating public officials and had other motives. It was still unconfirmed whether the deceased was pushed down by Gong. The police immediately dispatched officers to the countryside to arrest him, but Gong had already fled in fear and disappeared without a trace. The police ordered the deceased's family to return first and immediately summoned the local bailiffs Chen Zhixiang and Zhao Musheng to report to the court to send someone to open the coffin for an autopsy in order to apprehend the murderer and investigate the case.
